Unfortunate Shipping Incidents on the Yangtze 115

▲Groundings, Reef Impacts, Bandit Encounters, Collisions

Due to the cold weather and shallow waters on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River recently, several vessels belonging to Jardine Matheson, Nisshin Kisen, and China Merchants S.N. Co. have run aground or encountered bandits near Yichang. Furthermore, numerous sea-going vessels have also been involved in accidents due to fog. The news received yesterday is detailed below:

▲Wuling Maru (Nisshin Kisen) The Nisshin Kisen's Wuling Maru, while traveling near Tiaoguan, ran aground at the Tiaoguan entrance due to heavy snowfall obscuring the channel. Bandits on both banks immediately dispatched small boats to loot the vessel. Fortunately, soldiers of the guard detachment stationed on the ship opened fire with machine guns, repelling the bandits. The Yichang branch of Nisshin Kisen has already dispatched a vessel for rescue.

▲Wuxing (San Peh Steam Navigation Co.) The San Peh Steam Navigation Co.'s Wuxing encountered bandits firing upon the vessel from the riverbank near Changshou. Fortunately, due to the distance, no one was harmed. The Wuxing quickly reversed and retreated, heading towards Yichang. However, while navigating a shoal, the ship's bow struck a reef and was holed, narrowly avoiding disaster. A telegram yesterday reported minor repairs, and the vessel has since arrived in Yichang.

▲Yiling (China Merchants S.N. Co.) The China Merchants S.N. Co.'s Shanghai-Yichang route vessel, the Yiling, was fired upon by bandits on both banks in the Jidu area. Fortunately, the vessel quickly escaped without any injuries, but the ship's hull sustained damage.

▲Jiang He (Jardine Matheson) The Jardine Matheson's Jiang He ran aground near Xinlongtan, reportedly suffering damage to the hull, creating a dangerous situation. Before rescue ships dispatched by the Hankou branch arrived, local bandits gathered and began firing upon the vessel. Passengers took cover on the cabin floor. During this crisis, a Hankou tugboat arrived, and a British naval vessel also came to provide protection, causing the bandits to retreat. It was reported yesterday that the ship has been rescued.

▲Yuanjiang Maru (Nisshin Kisen) According to a telegram from Hankou received yesterday, the cargo in the bow compartment of the Yuanjiang Maru, which ran aground near Jiayu, has been unloaded by tugboats. All passengers have been transferred to the Dangyang Maru for transport to Yichang. The Yuanjiang Maru was rescued yesterday and is expected to arrive today.

▲Ning Shao (Ning Shao Steamship Company) The Ning Shao Steamship Company's Yangtze River vessel, the Ning Shao, encountered fog outside the Wusong estuary during its voyage from Shanghai. While at anchor, it was struck by an Asiatic Petroleum Company oil tanker. The Ning Shao's bow and rudder blade were damaged, but fortunately, the collision was relatively light, with only the iron plating of the bow dented and no breaches. The cargo was undamaged, and the passengers were safe. However, due to the rudder damage, the vessel was difficult to maneuver and, after negotiations with Asiatic Petroleum, returned to Shanghai, docking at Pier 16. The cargo was unloaded, a report was filed with the River Conservancy Bureau for inspection, and a claim was submitted to Asiatic Petroleum. Yesterday, Asiatic Petroleum replied to the Ning Shao Steamship Company, stating that they had not yet received a report from the ship's owner and were therefore unable to negotiate. All cargo and passengers were transferred to San Peh and Taikoo vessels today for transport to Hankou.

▲Weisheng (Jardine Matheson) The Jardine Matheson's Weisheng was carrying a large consignment of goods from Shanghai to Shantou, Guangzhou, and Hong Kong for unloading. Numerous passengers were also aboard, heading to various ports in Southeast Asia. The vessel's departure from Shanghai was delayed due to heavy fog. After the fog cleared and the ship left port, it was approaching the first lighthouse outside Wusong when an unidentified British vessel (name unknown) emerged from the fog, heading into the Huangpu River. Although the fog had lifted, visibility was still limited. The two vessels were on a collision course, and it was not until they were very close that they sighted each other. The Weisheng urgently sounded its whistle, requesting the approaching vessel to give way, but the other vessel's speed was too great, and a collision was unavoidable. The sea-going vessel struck the bow of the Weisheng. The shipmaster quickly reversed to avoid further damage. The Weisheng sustained damage. The shipmaster reassured the passengers, turned the vessel around, and returned to Shanghai, docking at the Gonghexing Wharf. He immediately reported the incident to the head office and customs, who boarded the vessel for inspection. Fortunately, the damage was above the waterline, allowing for immediate repairs in Shanghai. The cargo was undamaged. After a two-day delay in Shanghai, the vessel departed for Guangdong yesterday afternoon after completing essential repairs to the bow.

▲Old Taikoo vessel (Eurylohus) The British Old Taikoo Company's Eurylohus, after transporting goods from Lvfotuan to Japan and unloading them, reloaded cargo for Shanghai. While sailing to Sanjia Water near Wusong, it encountered heavy fog. The ship dropped anchor to wait for the fog to clear. Once the fog lifted, the vessel resumed its voyage to Shanghai. At Sanjia Water, less than half an hour into its voyage, it encountered the Norwegian vessel Litiopia, en route from New York via the Suez Canal and Hong Kong to Shanghai for unloading and outbound cargo. The Litiopia was sailing out of Shanghai. The Litiopia quickly maneuvered to avoid a head-on collision, but the Eurylohus sustained damage on the side of the forehold, while the Litiopia was damaged at the bow. Both vessels have now entered port.

▲Kinzan Maru (Nisshin Kisen) The Nisshin Kisen's Kinzan Maru struck a reef outside Shantou. The company received a follow-up telegram stating that the ship's hull and cargo have been completely abandoned as unsalvageable. Therefore, the Soshan Maru is still recovering the crew's belongings and some cargo from the deck to be transported back to Shanghai. The Soshan's departure date will be delayed by four days.

▲Yichang (China Merchants S.N. Co.) The China Merchants S.N. Co.'s motor vessel, the Yichang, struck a submerged reef 50 miles from the mouth of the Huangpu River, sustaining severe damage. Due to the dangerous situation, the shipmaster intentionally grounded the vessel on a shoal to prevent total loss. The vessel was en route from Chongqing, carrying valuable merchandise and an unknown number of passengers. It is reported that the forehold is flooded, potentially damaging the cargo. The company dispatched the vessel Victoria yesterday morning to provide assistance. This vessel is one of the newest and most modern on the river, and its shipmaster, Mr. Micklos, is an experienced navigator. The vessel and cargo are reportedly insured.

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Investigates Railway Freight Rates for Various Industries 116

▲Preparing to Submit to the National Freight Rate Conference

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a circular yesterday to 53 trade associations, including cotton textile, cigarette, silk, soap, machinery, egg, timber, and cotton cloth, stating: "Regarding the Chamber's previous proposal for encouraging and protecting domestic industries, submitted to the Ministry of Industry, we received a reply on January 21st with document number Shang Zi 805, acknowledging receipt. The Ministry is currently reviewing the status of various domestic enterprises and preparing relevant measures. The opinions submitted will be considered. Regarding the proposal to reduce freight rates for domestic goods compared to similar foreign goods, the National Freight Rate Conference convened by the Ministry of Railways will open on March 15th. Please prepare proposals in advance and submit them directly to the Ministry of Railways for discussion at the conference." Therefore, to protect domestic goods, please provide a systematic report comparing domestic goods with foreign goods for which competition exists and the freight rates for domestic and foreign goods. The National Railway Freight Rate Conference is imminent, and few responses have been received to previous requests for relevant information. Please provide detailed reports on foreign goods with which competition exists and the freight rates for domestic and foreign goods to the Chamber by March 15th for review. Do not delay."

Actual Situation of Meningitis in Shanghai 117

▲Not Yet in an Epidemic State

The Municipal Health Bureau, from January of this year to date, has received dozens of reports from hospitals and citizens regarding cases of epidemic cerebrospinal meningitis. After thorough investigation, it has been confirmed that there are 12 cases, with four deaths. The mortality rate is alarming. Fortunately, the cases are scattered and have not yet reached an epidemic state. However, in light of the rampant epidemic in Zhejiang and to prevent the disease from entering the city, preventive vaccinations have been implemented. Personnel have been dispatched daily to administer injections. In four days, 4,936 people have been vaccinated. Technical staff have also been dispatched to inspect the conditions of patients' homes and implement disinfection.

Extension of Tallying Hours for Money Shops During Account Closing Period 118

Money shops normally operate during fixed hours daily. However, during the current account closing period, procedures are more complex, often causing delays. Therefore, a temporary measure has been implemented for the current account closing period. From February 10th to 14th, the tallying time for fellow businesses will be extended to 4 PM (compared to the usual 2 PM; items received after the normal time will be processed the following day). Rejected tallies must be handled by 8 PM. These changes do not apply to non-business transactions. On February 15th, the tallying time will be extended to 10 PM, and on February 16th, to 5 PM. During the account closing period, the market for silver exchange rates will remain open as usual.

Currently, the business is affected by the trend of women cutting their hair, and most workers have changed careers, leaving only shop employees to maintain union affairs, making reorganization impossible.

Record of the Meeting of the China Industrial and Commercial Management Association 120

▲Kong Xiangxi to Speak Today on the Promotion of the Factory Law

The China Industrial and Commercial Management Association held its sixth board meeting yesterday afternoon at the Lianhua General Association to discuss future development plans. Board members present included Liu Hongsheng, Xu Jizhi, Hu Shuhua, and Shou Yicheng. The Secretary-General Cao first reported on the work plan, which was divided into the following four items: (1) Hold a dinner discussion meeting, inviting all members to participate in the discussion of major issues related to the industrial and commercial community. (2) Establish a special consulting committee for industrial and commercial management, hiring experts in engineering, economics, accounting, law, personnel administration, and other fields to serve as advisors to the committee for consultation by the industrial and commercial community. (3) Conduct investigations by sending personnel to the factories managed by various members for on-site investigations to gather research data. (4) Publish periodicals, both regular and irregular, dedicated to scientific management and related articles for reference by the industrial and commercial community. After detailed discussion by the board members, the plan was deemed appropriate. The dates, topics, and speakers for the dinner meeting were decided, and the secretariat was instructed to proceed actively. It is reported that the association has scheduled its first dinner discussion meeting for 1:00 PM today at the Lianhua General Association, inviting Minister of Industry Kong Xiangxi to speak on "How We Should Promote the Factory Law and How to Overcome the Difficulties in Implementing the Factory Law." All members are expected to participate, and a grand occasion is anticipated.

The Shanghai Executive Committee Requests Preferential Treatment for Liu Rongtai 121

▲Letter to the Two-Route Railway Administration for Review

The entire staff of the Fire Brigade, due to the tragic death of Liu Rongtai in the line of duty, submitted a request on the first of this month to the Sixth District Party Department to forward it to higher authorities, appealing for assistance. The Shanghai Executive Committee, upon receiving the request, determined that Liu's unfortunate demise was due to the railway gate not being closed and the negligence of railway personnel. Subsequently, railway staff obstructed rescue efforts, leading to his death from exposure. The Railway Bureau should be held responsible. Furthermore, Liu was serving on a voluntary basis in the public interest, making his case unlike other accidental tragedies. The 85th Executive Committee Standing Committee resolved to send a letter to the Two-Route Railway Administration, requesting preferential compensation to console his spirit. It is anticipated that the Railway Administration will take appropriate action upon receiving the letter.

The French Concession Authorities Punish Unregistered Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioners 125

▲National Medicine Association Sends Letter to the French Municipal Council to Discuss the Matter

The French Concession is holding registration affairs of doctors, and it has been announced on Western newspapers for a while. The Chinese people did not know about it, so the French Concession authorities removed the signs of many of the Chinese medicine practitioners and brought them to the police office for punishment. As a result, the Chinese medicine community started to feel upset and reported to the National Medicine Association. Now, the National Medicine Association sends a letter to the Hygiene Department of the French Municipal Council as following: Dear sirs, our Association is the only legal group organized by qualified traditional Chinese medicine practitioners in Shanghai who have registered with the Hygiene Bureau. The association has registered with various party and government organs. Recently, our members residing in the French Concession reported to the association that they have not received any formal notification or seen any official announcement regarding the recent registration of doctors in the French Concession. As a result, the authorities have sent personnel to impose penalties, which is akin to punishing without warning. The members involved are understandably alarmed. After contacting the association, we found the regulations for doctor registration in the French Concession, which demonstrates your bureau's intention to rectify the situation regarding doctors and prioritize the lives of the people. We deeply admire this. However, as these regulations are still in their early stages of implementation, there are three points that should be handled with flexibility: (1) Most doctors are not yet fully aware of this registration matter. Within three months, penalties should be temporarily suspended for those who have not yet completed the procedures and obtained a license. (2) Doctors from outside the concession who come to the French Concession for consultation should be exempt from obtaining a license, as doctors from outside the concession who do not have formal medical qualifications are already subject to suppression (registration has been completed in the Chinese-administered area, and registration will be held in the Public Concession), so those who are able to practice medicine in the French Concession should have the qualifications already and it is unnecessary to register repeatedly to save the procedures. (3) The registration fee should only be paid once, as the services provided by doctors are related to the lives of people within the concession and public health, which cannot be compared to commercial activities such as vegetable vendors' permits or vehicle permits, which require regular fees. Even Chinese government authorities only charge registration fees once. We hope that the above three points will be adopted by your bureau to avoid disputes and prevent unfortunate incidents. We sincerely hope that the bureau will take appropriate actions and revert to us to be appreciated.

National Medicine Museum Announces Meeting Date by Telegram 126

▲March 15th

The national medical and pharmaceutical community, in light of the gradual decline of Chinese medicine, urgently needs to promote it for revitalization. The National Medical and Pharmaceutical Organizations Joint Federation previously requested the government to establish a National Medicine Museum, which was approved by the Central Political Council. The preparatory office has been established and a general meeting will be held on March 15th to legally establish the Shanghai General Federation and the Shanghai National Medicine Association. The Shanghai General Federation and the Shanghai National Medicine Association have received the telegram, transcribed below: "Our country’s medicine originated in ancient times, seeking the truth. However, the essence of it is not well publicized and the Central Political Council resolved to establish a museum to organize the inherent culture with scientific methods. We request medical and pharmaceutical representatives from each province and city (3-5 persons per province, 2-1 persons per city and 1-2 persons per organization) to attend. The travel expenses for the delegates of each province, city and county medical groups are responsible. We will discuss the methods of advancing and indicate everything. With the effort of everyone, the study would not be in extinction. We are looking forward to meeting you.

The Termination of Shanghai Chen Da Cloth Factory is settled through mediation 129

Because the Chen Da Cloth Factory on Kang Ti Road will be terminated on the year-end day of the old calander, all the workers filed a lawsuit at the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to seek relief. The Bureau sent the order to the Factory that private termination is not allowed. After the Factory received the notice, it forced all the workers to leave the factory within 4 days. As a result, the workers filed a lawsuit for help again. The Bureau sent personnel to investigate. Yesterday at 9 a.m., the factory's representative Xu Qianyi, the employee's representative Lu Wancheng and Cheng Wentian went to the Bureau with Wang Bing as the chairman, to mediate on the case. The factory's representative required approval to terminate the factory because of bad business operation. The employee's representative agreed to terminate employment relationships because they have bad relation with the factory. Later, all the representatives from both sides agreed and signed the following agreement: The Chen Da Cloth Factory is allowed to be closed. The male and female workers like Cheng Wentian each get six yuan for the expenses to go home. The factory is allowed to terminate the employment. The room fees for the workers living in the factory is not deducted from the first day to the fifth day of the month. The chairman announced the mediation is settled.

Xiping County, Henan Province, Suffers Disaster and Awaits Relief 130

▲Red Cross Society Receives Telegram Requesting Relief

The Chinese Red Cross Society has received a telegram from the Henan Relief Association, forwarded from the Xiping County Magistrate's Disaster Investigation Committee, stating: "To the Chinese Red Cross Society: We are reporting from the Xiping County Magistrate, Pei Ran, and the Disaster Investigation Committee, Rou Hongjun. Since 1927, bandits have been rampant and floods have occurred repeatedly, resulting in property losses of over 30 million yuan and casualties of over 8,000 people. With the end of the war against Tang, we hoped to recuperate and recover slightly. However, the war broke out again in the spring, with Xiping County close to the front lines. Added to this, the bandits and communists are still rampaging. From July to October, the civilian casualties have totaled over 2,100 people, with over 1,900 people fleeing and over 1,500 houses burned. The requisition of cash, grain, firewood, and other supplies amounts to over 280,000 yuan, with indirect losses not included. Now, with the cold weather and the end of the year, the disaster victims are scattered everywhere, and the misery is unbearable to witness. We earnestly request relief." As Xiping is close to the battlefront, the vast amounts of supplies have been creating a great burden. After these pains, the remaining people are awaiting relief. In addition to having the association provide immediate aid and comfort, we request your compassion to provide relief to the disaster victims as soon as possible.

Page 15

Local News II

Detailed Record of Lu Yifang's Appeal in the Hu Die Trial 131

▲ Over Two Hundred Men and Women Attended

▲ Lu Used Chiang Kai-shek as an Analogy

▲ Jiang Yiping Speaks with Hu Die

▲ Lu Said Hu Die's Father Should Have a Conscience

The "Ling Bao" newspaper published an article titled "Record of Snow and Butterfly's Marriage and Separation" on the 3rd of the month. Film actress Hu Die believed that many statements in the article slandered her reputation. She hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to send a letter to the newspaper's editor, Lu Yifang, requesting a correction. Although "Ling Bao" made a correction, they added the phrase "everything is recorded" in the correction. They also published a photo of film actor Zhu Fei, with a note stating he was a "key figure in Snow and Butterfly's divorce." Hu became even more angry and hired lawyer Zhan to file a lawsuit on her behalf, requesting that Lu be punished under Article 325 of the Criminal Code. After the conclusion of the initial trial by the Special District Court, Lu was sentenced to a fine of three hundred yuan. Lu then filed an appeal and was ordered to pay a bail of five hundred yuan while awaiting trial, as detailed in previous reports. Yesterday was the date for the hearing, and so at 4:30 PM, the case was heard in the first courtroom of the Special District Court by Judge Zhou, along with assessors Cheng and Xiao. The appellant, Hu Die, wearing a yellow woolen coat, arrived at court with her father at 2:30 PM to await the hearing. The appellant, Lu Yifang, also arrived around 3:00 PM. More than two hundred men and women were in attendance. The hearing began at 4:30 PM, and the proceedings were as follows:

▲ "Everything is Recorded" Expresses Admission of Error

Judge Zhou first asked both parties their ages and addresses. Then he asked Lu Yifang what position he held at "Ling Bao." Lu replied that he was the manager and editor. The judge then asked the reason for the appeal. Lu replied that the original judgment determined that he intentionally defamed Hu Die. However, he had never met Hu Die and had no intention of defaming her. The original judgment stated that he traveled back and forth from Wuxi and that at most it was one week. The original judgment also determined that he sent the draft, which did not match the facts. After returning to Wuxi, the editing duties were entrusted to a friend as an agent. The correction draft had many definitive words, which my friend had deleted quite a bit. After it was published, Hu sent a letter requesting it and it was immediately handled. As for the phrase "everything is recorded" in the correction draft, it expressed admission of error. The original judgment determined that this phrase was unfavorable to Hu. The above are all reasons for the appeal. The other dissenting points are described in detail in the appeal statement. Please let the court review it.

▲ Proofreader Not Employed by Ling Bao

Judge Zhou then asked who submitted the article published on the 5th. Lu replied that he did not know. He only knew that his pseudonym was "King Kong." He did not know his address. He asked if "Ling Bao" should have rewarded the contributor after the manuscript was published. Lu replied that small newspapers were different from large newspapers. Most contributors to small newspapers are not paid. Moreover, this person also contributed to other newspapers. He asked how he knew. Lu replied that he also had his pseudonym in other newspapers, so he found out. He asked where the original manuscript was. Lu replied that the original manuscript was kept by the proofreader. Since this case occurred, the original proofreader has not been employed by "Ling Bao." He asked when he returned to Wuxi. Lu replied the 28th of November. He asked how many days away from the date of publication of this draft. Lu replied seven or eight days. He asked that you said two or three days in the first trial. Why do you say seven or eight days now? Lu replied that I said two or three issues in the first trial. He asked that according to you, two or three issues, two issues are six days, and three issues are nine days, which is also incorrect. He also asked what time he returned to Shanghai. Lu replied that on the 7th, he received Hu's letter requesting a correction that night, and it was too late on the 8th, so he corrected it on the 11th.

▲ Hard-working, Humorous Everyone

He asked, if you had added a statement when you corrected it, "I was away and a friend negligently published it," it would have been fine. Why did you add the sentence "everything is recorded?" According to your meaning, is it impossible to not record if you heard it? He also asked why Zhu Fei's photo was published on December 14, with the note "Key figure in Snow and Butterfly's divorce."

What does it mean? Lu replied that the photo was posted by the proofreader and had no meaning. As for the numbers next to the photo, it is a common practice, just like "hard-working Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek or humorous Wu Zhihui." He asked, had he been to Hu's house before publishing the article? Lu replied that he had not. He asked, but her father said that you went there and that you told him that you could help and asked them to subsidize some. Lu replied that he had never seen her father in his life. Everything he said was nonsense. If he had been there, he should have taken his business card. He asked, the article said that Hu had once entered the demimonde and worked as a small star. Do you know if she did it? Lu replied, I don't know.

▲ Hu Die Denies Ever Being a Concubine

Judge Zhou then turned to Hu Die. He asked, who is Lin Xuehuai to you? She replied, my fiancé. Have you had a contract termination? She replied, yes. He asked, why did you terminate the contract? She replied, because Lin wrote to me, saying that my reputation was not good and asked to terminate the contract with me. He asked, later, did you want him to terminate the contract, or did he want you to terminate the contract? She replied, he wanted to terminate the contract. He asked, do you and Lin often communicate? She replied, it's been six years. He asked, why did you sue Lu Yifang? She replied, Lu published defamatory material about my reputation in "Ling Bao," so I sued him. The article said that I entered the demimonde and was a concubine, which were untrue. It also said that my father was dead, relying on the Lin family for a living. My father is in court now. Isn't what the article says a joke? He asked, did Lu come to your house? She replied, he came, but I was not at home. My father received him. Lu said he could help and asked my father for a subsidy. He asked, when did he come? How do you know? She replied, he came on the evening of the 29th. My father told me.

▲ Jiang Yiping Questions Hu Die

At this point, Jiang Yiping, the appellant's representative lawyer, stood up and asked the court to ask Hu Die questions. The court permitted it, and Jiang then said to Hu, before this case was filed, Lu Yifang had come to your house twice to ask for subsidies. Did you mention this when you entrusted Lawyer Zhan to send a letter of correction? Hu replied that she did not. Jiang then asked, Lu happened to return to Wuxi when the article was published, and someone came to court to testify on his behalf. Can you provide evidence that Lu did not return to Wuxi? Hu replied that she could not prove whether or not she returned to Wuxi. Jiang then asked, since you didn't mention it and can't prove it, why did you only sue for defamation instead of suing for extortion when you filed the lawsuit? Hu replied, although Lu asked for it, I didn't suffer any loss, so I didn't sue. The defamatory article was published in the newspaper, and my reputation has been damaged, so I sued.

▲ There are Many Other Terrible Words in the Original Manuscript

The court also summoned witness Xie Hequn and ordered Xie to make an oath and said that he must be responsible for what he said after the oath. Xie testified that he was a friend of Lu and that he worked in a newspaper. When he arrived in Shanghai, Lu happened to have something to do and returned to Wuxi, so he entrusted me to edit "Ling Bao" on his behalf, from November 27 to December 7, for about three or four issues. The manuscript was an external contribution. There were many other terrible words in the original manuscript. For the sake of prudence and for the sake of Hu's reputation, I have deleted a lot of it, and then published it as a kind of rumored news. As for what happened after the 7th, I don't know.

▲ Don't Know Where Original Manuscript is Hidden

After Xie's testimony, Judge Zhou asked Lu Yifang when he returned to Shanghai from Wuxi. Lu replied on the 7th and said that he had been in the news business for many years and knew the situation of running a newspaper. This time, he really did not intend to defame Hu. He asked if the original could be retrieved now. Lu replied that the manuscript was kept by the proofreader and now he did not know where it was hidden. He asked, is what you said true? He replied, it is true.

▲ Eloquence of Lawyers Jiang and Zhang

At this point, Judge Zhou announced that the lawyers from both sides would begin to debate. First, Jiang Yiping stood up and said that Lu Yifang had just gone to Wuxi when "Ling Bao" published the manuscript, and Xie Hequn came to court to testify. Hu could not prove that Lu was still in Shanghai. Xie was able to come to court to testify for Lu, so the truth of the matter can be imagined. Lu was not in Shanghai, so he had no intention of defaming him and should not bear criminal responsibility. Even if there is criminal liability, it should be borne by the agent. Moreover, according to the provisions of the Publication Law, once corrected, the responsibility can be exempted. As for the four words "everything is recorded," it was published to correct the error of the Hu Die incident, and it also means that the newspaper's records may be wrong, and cannot bear criminal responsibility. Also, the so-called "key figure" cannot be regarded as malicious or derogatory. The "key figure" refers to the person who mediates between the two parties, which is not impossible. Moreover, the original sentence of a fine of 300 yuan is a bit excessive, so our lawyer asks the judge to revoke the original sentence and declare the appellant innocent. After Jiang finished speaking, lawyer Zhang Chongding also stood up and said that lawyer Jiang had already explained the reasons for the appeal in detail. Now I will only add a little supplement. The "Ling Bao" newspaper run by the appellant is a type of newspaper. If it is punished according to Article 325 of the Criminal Law, it seems inappropriate. Also, the Publication Law is a special law. According to the application order, it should be punished according to the Publication Law first. Please judge the appellant not guilty.

▲ Dali Yuan Tong Zi No. 19

Hu Die's representative lawyer, Zhan Jifeng, stood up and replied that the original judgment of this case was very clear. There is no need to reply to the points mentioned by lawyers Jiang and Zhang, and there is no need to reply. However, there is one point in what lawyer Jiang said just now that is a reversal of the facts, and our lawyer cannot but reply, that is, lawyer Jiang said that there is a sentence "seems to be affected" in the letter of correction, but the original letter clearly stated "indeed suffered a great influence." The judge may wish to read it. As for the date of going to Wuxi provided by the appellant, it also does not match before and after. It can be seen that his intention is nothing more than to shirk responsibility. As for the Publication Law cited, it said that after the correction, he will not be held responsible, can it overthrow the Criminal Law? According to Dali Yuan precedent Tong Zi No. 19, even if it has been corrected, it still cannot be exempt from criminal liability. Please reject the appeal and uphold the original judgment. After speaking, he presented a large book of Dali Yuan Tong Zi No. 19 to the court for review. Finally, lawyer Shi Lin represented the appellant and rebutted Lu Yifang's four grounds of appeal one by one. After the debate was over,

▲ Hu Die Asked to Uphold the Original Judgment

Judge Zhou then asked Hu Die if she had anything to say. Hu replied, please uphold the original judgment. He also asked, did you see Lu come to your house? She replied that her father told her that Lu went to my house on the evening of November 29 to ask for a subsidy. I believe my father would not lie to me.

▲ Yifang Denies Extortionary Behavior

Judge Zhou then asked Lu Yifang if he had anything to say. Lu answered at length, saying briefly that the other party accused me of intentional defamation. It should be judged whether I have been to Hu's house or not. I don't know Hu and his father, not even the direction of their home. How can I ask them for extortion? And the matter of Hu and Lin's termination of the contract has been rumored at sea, and there is nothing to hide. Therefore, there is no room for extortion in the first place. Hu's father's words, for those who are slightly knowledgeable, can be understood without thinking. It's all made up. I have always known how to love myself. Everyone I associate with is deeply aware. How can I risk this injustice and ask people for extortion? Even if I don't feel sorry for myself, I should feel sorry for my friends in general. Also, Hu's father said that on November 29, I went to his house with several companions under the pretext of interviewing, and on the 1st, I went alone to ask for a subsidy. Hu Die said that she had already asked for a subsidy on the 29th. The statements are inconsistent and can be generally seen. Also, I am still young and will plan to establish myself in society in the future and will never do this bad behavior.

▲ Hu's Father Speaks with White-Haired Conscience

Now Hu's father is old with white hair. He should speak with conscience in this court. Otherwise, he will not be subject to the restraint of conscience. I have no intention of defamation and no malice towards others. Please ask the judge to revoke the original sentence. After Lu finished speaking, Judge Zhou announced that the debate in the case was over and the sentence would be pronounced at 2 pm on the 13th. Then the court adjourned.

Clearing of Debts of Day and Night Bank Distributed to Shareholders 132

▲ Auditor Urges Collection by Letter Again

In the case of the liquidation of Day and Night Bank and the Great World Tourist Savings Department, the French Concession Court has appointed auditors Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang to be responsible for handling it. At the same time, the municipal government has also stated that it will maintain it. The following are the reports from yesterday:

▲ Creditors Petition

Around 4 pm yesterday, a temporary committee of creditors sent three representatives to the municipal government to petition and submit a supplementary submission, requesting the municipal government to take the lead in convening a joint meeting to handle the liquidation as soon as possible to protect the savings of the depositors. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun received him and talked for about 20 minutes. According to the reporter's investigation, the municipal government is now discussing a proper solution with all parties. It is expected that a decision will be made within a few days.

▲ Auditor's Opinion

Yesterday, this reporter interviewed auditor Wu Zheng, who was handling the liquidation. According to him, regarding the business operations of the stores under Gongfa Company, everything is being investigated in detail. It is expected that the debts of the Chinese and Western pharmacies and hot spring locker rooms can be paid off. The Great World owes the Day and Night Bank more than 600,000 yuan, and the Tourist Savings Department owes more than 600,000 yuan, for a total debt of about 1.2 million yuan. It is not easy to pay it off immediately, but it is not difficult to gradually clear it with the profits earned over time. Although Fuchang Tobacco Company is more difficult, it is hoped that it can be reorganized. What should be clear now is how much Huang Chujiu's estate has and whether it can repay the Day and Night Bank's debt of 1.05 million yuan. Today (i.e. yesterday), we have sent a letter to lawyer Tan Yigong to ask for the estate registration form so that there is a real basis. The list of shareholders of Gongfa Company and the stock sample should also be investigated clearly. According to Mr. Yuan Lvdeng, it has been handed over to auditor Xu Yongzuo, but Mr. Xu said in a letter that it is still in the Aftermath Committee, so today (i.e. yesterday) we have also sent a letter to the committee to urge them to collect it. This matter will eventually come to light. After the shareholder list and the estate registration form are obtained, we can start to prepare a liquidation plan report and submit it to the French Concession Court for review.

▲ Pan Gongzhan's Conversation

Yesterday, the reporter made a special visit to Director Pan of the Social Affairs Bureau to ask for details. (Question) It is said that the municipal government will take the lead in handling this case. Is this true? (Answer) This case involves more than 13,000 depositors, with deposits totaling more than 2 million yuan, mostly from poor people's hard-earned money. This long delay is not a good plan. The municipal government is paying close attention to it. However, some creditors have filed a lawsuit with the French Concession Court, which has been accepted, and someone has been sent to keep the account books, and there is also an injunction of provisional attachment. It is heard that another group of creditors has filed a lawsuit with the Special District Court of the Public Concession. If it is accepted separately like this, it will inevitably become more chaotic and there will be no way to solve it. However, since the judicial organs have accepted the case first, if the outside world wants the administrative organs to handle it, it must go through considerable steps: (1) the creditors should submit a petition to the municipal government for a complete liquidation so that they can plan comprehensively, or (2) the debtors, i.e. the board of directors or shareholders' meeting of Gongfa Company, should submit a petition to the municipal government to take the lead in sending personnel to liquidate. If one of these conditions is met, the municipal government can probably follow the public opinion and handle it impartially. Otherwise, it seems that the municipal government is not convenient to participate in cases that are already in court. (Question) If the municipal government takes the lead in handling it in the future, will the Social Affairs Bureau handle the liquidation? (Answer) If the situation is such that the municipal government has to take the lead, the municipal government will probably send a liquidator. The Social Affairs Bureau has a lot of daily business and it is not convenient to directly handle the liquidation for a company's debt dispute. (Question) Is the name of the directors and shareholders of Gongfa Company who should be liquidated available for examination? (Answer) The directors of Gongfa Company should have come out and taken responsibility for handling it a long time ago. It is a pity that they have been unheard of for many days, which is not appropriate. The names of the directors and supervisors have been secretly investigated as follows: (Directors) Huang Chujiu, Yuan Lvdeng, Ye Shantao, Zhao Qinbo, Cao Binchen, Dai Jiezai, Zhou Songqing, etc. (Supervisors) Chen Xingwu, Zhang Huizan. As for the shareholder list, it is still being secretly investigated. (Question) What will be the liquidation policy in the future? (Answer) How to liquidate is a question for the future. However, the sole purpose of the government's supervision of liquidation is to prevent creditors from suffering losses, especially to prevent small depositors from suffering losses. To achieve this goal, we must (1) order the directors and shareholders to bear full responsibility, (2) formulate a liquidation plan as soon as possible, (3) the affiliated business institutions of Gongfa Company, such as those that can be maintained, should be maintained immediately, otherwise they will all collapse one by one, and it will be even more unthinkable, and the creditors will suffer even greater losses, (4) all of Huang Chujiu's private property should be liquidated and used to offset his outstanding debts. (Question) Can the people who owe Gongfa Company offset the debts they owe? (Answer) It is difficult to say this. The detailed accounts need to be liquidated. If it is not enough, of course the directors and shareholders will be responsible. However, it is estimated that the savings deposits received by Day and Night Bank and the Great World Savings Department amount to 3 million yuan. If the company can handle it well, it is not impossible to repay. Such as (1) the right to use the land and buildings of the Great World, if it continues to operate, or if the remaining 30-year lease right is transferred, it is heard that it is worth 800,000 to 1 million yuan, (2) the Chinese and Western pharmacies and their branches, based on their current business situation, are profitable every year, and it is heard that they are worth 250,000 yuan, (3) the hot spring bathhouse is heard to be worth 50,000 yuan, (4) Fuchang Tobacco Company, together with the Three Film Company, if it continues to operate, the trademarks and goods are heard to be

Page 16

It can be worth about 500,000 to 600,000 yuan. The above is worth about 2 million yuan in total. The only thing missing is more than 1 million yuan, which is the money Huang Chujiu personally owes the Day and Night Bank. However, according to yesterday's newspaper report, lawyer Tan Yigong said that Huang's antiques, jade articles, calligraphy, paintings, and other family properties and houses are worth about 1 million taels, which is enough to offset all kinds of debts. Although it is not yet convenient to believe whether it is true, there are always some results that are not far off. If there is still not enough, then each director will be responsible for compensating for the amount that is not much, and the managers of the affiliated business institutions have a deep friendship with Huang and will give some assistance to Li Chu for the sake of the aftermath. If all parties can write their duties and there is a unified management agency, it is not difficult to have a better result, although it may not be as satisfactory as everyone wants. It is better than the current panic.

Record of the Trial of Xia Shaoen, the Murderer in the Zhao Assassination Case 133

▲ Bodyguard and Chauffeur Testify in Court

▲ Xia Confesses, Then Retracts, Awaiting Retrial

In the case of the assassination of Zhao Tieqiao, the general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Xia Shaoen was captured by the Shanghai County Public Security Bureau, and Wang Jinshan (i.e. Wang Laosan) and Cheng Haibo were captured by the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau. The Executive Yuan ordered them to be sent to the Shanghai Local Court for trial. Xia Shaoen was sent to the court at the end of last year, so the prosecutor investigated him first and filed a public prosecution against him for the crime of premeditated murder.

▲ Testimony of Bodyguard Liu Hua

Yesterday morning, Judge Zhao Tieqiao opened the first courtroom for trial and first interrogated the witnesses. According to Zhao's bodyguard, Liu Hua, on the day of the incident, at 9:00 am, because his wife wanted to buy things at the New New Company, they went together. I sat with the chauffeur Shen Ashan to the front of the General Bureau. I got out of the car first. The general manager got out of the car and went inside. I was closing the car door when I heard a gunshot. I turned around and saw a person walking out of it, wearing a striped short shirt. I forgot what color the stripes were. His pants were either blue or black, and I don't remember. At this time, a person wearing a blue short shirt and pants shot at me, piercing the leather bag I was carrying. I blew the police whistle. He asked where the general manager was shot. He replied that the bullet entered the right waist and exited the front chest.

▲ Testimony of Chauffeur Shen Ashan

The chauffeur Shen Ashan also testified that he went to Zhao's office in January of the 18th year of the Republic of China and was paid 35 yuan per month. On the day of the incident, there were three people in the car, one general manager, one wife, and one bodyguard sitting next to me. The car stopped, and the general manager got out and went inside. I was looking at the car door when I heard a sound, which I thought was a rickshaw tire blowing out. At this time, I heard the wife say that something had happened to the general manager. I turned around and looked inside. I saw the general manager running up the escalator. At that time, a man in a striped cloth shirt was holding a gun and fleeing towards the Puxi side. I blew the police whistle. Then I heard another gunshot. I looked back and saw that the bodyguard had fallen to the ground. I saw that this person was of medium height and had a black face. When I parked the car, there was a man in a black long shirt with a small face next to the car, but I didn't pay attention. Later, Section Chief Zhang helped the general manager from the escalator into the car and sent him to Baolong Hospital. The wife got out of the car and stayed at the bureau. I went with the bodyguard. When the car arrived at Xizang Road, Zhao suddenly asked if you knew where Mr. Fan Zhengbo was treated before. I said I knew it was the Red Cross, so I immediately turned to the Red Cross.

▲ Testimony of Miscellaneous Servants and Patrolmen

According to Wu Deshan, a servant at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, I am a servant who opens the door and sweeps the floor. On the day of the incident, I was inside, so I didn't know. According to Wang Shifu, the gatekeeper, I heard a gunshot and the general manager went upstairs. At that time, I thought the tire had blown out. When I heard the second sound, I ran out. The bodyguard had fallen to the ground, and the murderer was gone. I am in charge of the front door. There are four of us colleagues, one at the front door, one at the back door, one in the general manager's office, and one on the night shift.

▲ Xia Shaoen's Confession

At this point, the official ordered Xia Shaoen to be brought to court. According to his confession, he is 36 years old, from Hefei, Anhui, and lives at No. 1750 Yinghua Lane, Roberts Road. In the 15th year of the Republic of China, because his hometown was barren, he came to Shanghai with his mother and wife. He first sold vegetables. Later, a friend surnamed Wang recommended him to be a police officer in the Fifth District. Because he couldn't speak the local dialect, they thought he was stupid, so he quit after February. Later, he sold vegetables again. The following year, Gong Shaolan and Xu Caiyuan, fellow villagers, introduced me to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company as a soldier in the roving patrol team, with a monthly salary of 15 yuan. There were one or two hundred people in total, stationed in Pudong. I didn't have a gun. The captain's name was Hu Yuqing. It was disbanded in October of the 18th year. After that, he still worked as a vegetable seller. In June of last year, he went to Hefei for medical treatment due to illness and came out in September. Wang Laosan, who is now in the same case, met in March. Because he sold vegetables past his door, he knew that he was a fellow villager. The official asked if Wang Laosan called you to kill someone. He replied that it was not the case. He asked if you admitted in the Public Security Bureau that Wang Laosan called you to Shanghai from Anhui. You didn't have any money. He bought you two yuan of rice and gave you a box gun. You said that if you killed someone, you would have to pay with your life. He said that if you didn't kill someone, you wouldn't thrive, and you would kill your whole family. How do you explain this? He replied that he was forced to confess after being beaten severely. He asked how you admitted it three times in the Procuratorate of this court. He replied that the secret agent told me to admit to it three times and was tricked by him. The official rebutted him again and ordered him to wait for retrial. The defendant was sent back to prison.

Mei Fei is Not Guilty 134

▲ Sentence in Appeal Case Announced Yesterday

In the case where prostitute Mei Fei was accused by Tan Meiying of colluding with Hu San to embezzle her husband Zhao Guangzu's land ownership form, the initial trial sentenced Mei Fei to two months' imprisonment with probation and ordered her to return the ownership form. Mei Fei refused to accept the judgment and hired lawyer Shen Xiangshan to file an appeal. In the meantime, because Tan and Zhao had a divorce lawsuit, the case was suspended. Recently, Tan and Zhao restored their relationship, and Tan appeared in court as the appellant. After the High Court's final hearing, the court opened yesterday afternoon, and Judge Song and assessors Zhu and Gao announced that the original judgment was revoked and Chen Junxia (Mei Fei) was not guilty. The judge was afraid that Tan Fang would not accept the judgment and would file a third-instance appeal, so he instructed Mei Fei to pay the original bail during the appeal period.

A Box of Mud Deceitfully Claimed to be Over Ten Thousand Silver Dollars 136

▲ Russian Con Man's Elaborate Scheme Failed

▲ Danish Woman Fortunately Not Fooled

A 35-year-old Russian con man named Robert Spier used a small wooden box containing mud, stones, and a large block of hardened cement weighing over sixty pounds. The box was sealed to resemble one shipped from another city. He transported it to an apartment rented by a Danish woman, Marna Snethlage Graham, located at No. 70, Lane 589, Route Lafayette in the French Concession. He told the landlady that he had just arrived in Shanghai from Harbin and that the box contained over ten thousand silver dollars. He asked for a receipt, saying he needed to go to the pier to retrieve his luggage. The landlady, believing him, wrote the receipt. Robert then pretexted that he was going to retrieve his luggage. Later that evening, he called the landlady from a store on Avenue Joffre, claiming that he was at the Jianghai Customs House retrieving his luggage and needed to pay over seven hundred silver dollars in customs fees, but was short one hundred ninety silver dollars. He asked if she could lend him the money, promising to return it upon his return to the apartment. The landlady replied that it was late and she didn't have that much money on hand. Robert was greatly disappointed. The landlady became suspicious when Robert did not return after a long time. She reported the matter to the French Concession police, who sent detectives to the apartment. They opened the wooden box and discovered the scam. The Western detectives apprehended Robert, and he was brought before the French court yesterday for questioning. The Western detective chief reported the details of the case and stated that the defendant had a prior record in the International Settlement. The plaintiff then recounted the details of the attempted fraud. When questioned, Robert Spier admitted his intention to deceive. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced the defendant to one month in the Western jail, followed by permanent expulsion from the French Concession.

Armed Robbery on Great West Road: Robbers Brought to Court Yesterday 137

▲ Two Killed the Night Before

▲ Woman Carrying Weapons for Robbers

▲ Robbers Committed Crimes in the City

▲ Public Safety Bureau Also Requested Transfer

Around 9 PM the previous night, a group of armed robbers broke into the Suzhou native Zhou Yuanxing's home at No. 1175, Westward Gate, and stole valuables worth over five thousand silver dollars before fleeing. Upon receiving the report, the Old Zhabei Police Department immediately dispatched Chinese detectives Song Bingzheng and Zhu Ziqing, among others, to intercept them. The robbers dared to open fire on the arresting officers, who returned fire. The exchange lasted about half an hour, resulting in the immediate deaths of robbers Ye Atai and another unidentified individual. Robbers Pang Zhenfang and Pei Yousan were wounded. Zhang Sihao, Zhu Yaoyue, Gao Weibao, Wang Heting, Yang Shaoqing, Ren Bingwen, Fu Zhongchen, Jiang Dekui, Tang Jingen, Zhang Xiaobazi, Xu Shixun, and women Zhu Zhangshi and Zhang Wangshi were apprehended. Two handguns and eight bullets were confiscated. This was reported in the press. Yesterday morning, the police escorted the captured robbers to the First Criminal Court of the Special District Court. Judge Xu Jiashi presided over the interrogation. Police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that around 8 PM the previous night, a gang of eight robbers invaded No. 1175 Great West Road. Four robbers, each armed with a handgun, silenced the occupants. Zhang Anbo secretly slipped out through the back door and reported to the nearby beat police, who relayed the message to the Old Zhabei Police Department. All detectives were ordered to apprehend the robbers, who opened fire to resist arrest. The detectives returned fire, resulting in the deaths of Ye Atai and an unidentified individual. Pang and Pei were captured. Jewelry and silver dollars worth over two thousand silver dollars were found on Pang. The remaining three thousand silver dollars were not recovered. A handgun with empty bullet casings was found in the hand of one of the dead robbers. Another handgun with eight bullets was found near the back door of No. 1176. Robber Pang Zhenfang confessed the location of his accomplices. Detectives went to Room 36 of the Huashang Hotel at No. 15 North Sea Road. Public Safety Bureau detectives were already present, claiming they had received a tip that robbers involved in robberies at No. 186 Qinglian Street and No. 32 Xingye Street in the city were there. The detectives arrested Zhang Sihao, who was identified by the plaintiffs as one of the robbers. The women Zhang Wangshi and others were found to be carrying weapons for the robbers. The Public Safety Bureau requested the transfer of the suspects, but the police department requested that the case be concluded before the transfer. Judge Xu, after verifying the confessions, ordered the defendants remanded in custody pending further investigation.

Spring Chill 138

The city has been shrouded in fog and haze for five consecutive days. Temperatures have been high, and the weather has been unusually warm. Around 8 PM the night before last, a sudden north wind arose, and the temperature dropped. The fog dissipated, and rain and snow fell intermittently overnight, clearing yesterday afternoon. The thermometer dropped to thirty-two degrees, the first cold snap since the beginning of spring.

Defendant Returned the Original Items

Qu Baozhen, a former dancer, recently hired lawyer Wu Shaoshan to sue Tao Naxun in the Special District Court for fraudulently obtaining gold, pearl, and diamond jewelry worth two thousand silver dollars. ▲ Feng Asan Wounded by Gangster

Educational News in Shanghai

Shanghai Municipal Council Discusses Chinese Education 155

▲ Many Favor Subsidizing Existing Schools

▲ Concrete Proposals to be Presented Before the Annual Meeting of Western Ratepayers

▲ Budget of at Least 250,000 Taels

▲ Increased Taxes Earmarked for Education

The China Press reports that the Shanghai Municipal Council, at its regular board meeting on Wednesday, meticulously discussed the Education Committee's ambitious plan to increase educational opportunities for Chinese residents in the Settlement and registered its approval in the minutes. However, as the plan would necessitate an increase in taxes, it will be submitted to the annual meeting of Western ratepayers for a decision. At the same time, the Council will announce in detail the reasons for its support to the Western ratepayers, so that the ratepayers may be more aware of the advantages and disadvantages of the plan. It is reported that during the board discussion of the matter, the issue of funding was considered at length. The chief accountant stated that the Council had many municipal projects within the Settlement requiring investment, and expenses were increasing daily. He believed that the required funds for the plan could only be met by increasing taxes. However, he did not support increasing taxes. He suggested accepting the principles of the plan but modifying its implementation. One director immediately objected, believing that the demand for the Council to provide educational opportunities for Chinese residents would eventually exceed the current plan and that increased taxes were the only way to meet this need. Another commissioner stated that Chinese ratepayers contributed a significant amount to educational funds within the Settlement, and the educational opportunities currently afforded to Chinese residents could not be considered adequate compensation for this contribution. As there was an urgent need to increase and expand educational opportunities, efforts should be made to meet their expectations. He had consulted with Chinese residents, who would not object to increased taxes if they were earmarked for educational purposes. Another commissioner suggested implementing the plan with the schools listed in this year's budget and submitting it to the Western ratepayers' meeting before fully adopting it. However, the Director-General disagreed, arguing that if the Western ratepayers rejected the plan, it would cause a backlash from the Chinese community and put the Council in a difficult position. After further discussion, it was decided to accept the principles of the plan and to publish its contents in detail before the Western ratepayers' annual meeting, clearly expressing the Council's support for the plan. The funds for the plan would be separated from ordinary government expenses and funded by increased taxes. Regarding the subsidy for existing schools, the chief accountant stated that the Education Committee had not yet proposed a specific amount. He tentatively listed 50,000 taels in the budget. One director stated that the Education Committee had expressed agreement in principle to first present concrete proposals and then prepare a budget. He estimated that the cost would be at least 250,000 taels. As a result, the directors largely favored subsidizing existing schools for economic reasons, thereby reducing capital expenditures on increasing educational opportunities.

Gu Shusen, Zhu Yingpeng, and Cen Dezhang Ordered to Take Over China Public School 156

▲ Scheduled to Receive it Today

▲ Ma Junwu Prepares to Hand Over

(Guomin News Agency) Following the student unrest at China Public School, the Ministry of Education dispatched personnel to investigate and then appointed Shang Shusen, Zhu Yingpeng, and Cen Dezhang as temporary takeover committee members to carry out reorganization. Some details were reported yesterday. We now understand that the three committee members, including Mr. Gu, received a directive from the Ministry of Education yesterday, along with the official seal of the committee's office, ordering them to take over the school as soon as possible. It is said that Mr. Gu and the others have decided to travel to Wusong this morning to take over the school. Ma Junwu has prepared to hand over the school and has appointed two staff members to handle the handover today. The original text of the Ministry of Education's directive to Gu Shusen, Zhu Yingpeng, and Cen Dezhang, as well as the rules of the committee's office, are recorded below:

▲ Directive from the Ministry of Education: Upon investigation, China Public School, a private institution, has experienced repeated disturbances in recent months. Since the board of directors approved Principal Ma Junwu's resignation, the school's internal affairs have disregarded the board's resolutions. Students have arbitrarily welcomed or rejected candidates for principal, and have formed illegal organizations to interfere with school affairs, even leading to fighting. The Ministry has repeatedly received orders from the Executive Yuan to investigate and handle the matter, and has also received reports and telegrams from various parties regarding the school's current situation. We have already dispatched personnel to the school to investigate. According to reports, the school has not followed the Ministry's orders regarding party education, and the students' thinking is complex, with factions and divisions. The school's internal order is chaotic, and it is almost in a state of being without leadership. Furthermore, according to a report from Cai Yuanpei, Chairman of the Board of Directors, and board members Gao Yihan, Wang Yunwu, Liu Binglin, Yang Xingfo, and Ding Yiyin, regarding the process of re-electing the principal, and noting that the school's disputes are worsening and that they cannot bear to sit idly by, nor can they maintain order, they have resigned from the board of directors. Upon reviewing the report, the school has not respected the board's resolutions and has rejected the board's takeover of the school. With such repeated disputes, discipline has been lost, the foundation of the school is shaken, and no one is taking responsibility. The school should be disbanded immediately. However, considering that the school has been established for over twenty years, we cannot allow the disturbances of a few individuals to cause the school to disappear. In addition to urging the resigning board members to consider the school's future and not to lose heart, we have formulated the "Rules of the Temporary Takeover Committee Office of China Public School," established the "Temporary Takeover Committee Office of China Public School," and appointed Gu Shusen, Zhu Yingpeng, and Cen Dezhang as temporary takeover committee members for the school, designating Gu Shusen as the permanent committee member, to temporarily take over the school and carry out reorganization. All school organizations and illegal groups will be disbanded. The contracts previously issued to the school's faculty and staff will be suspended. The start of the school term will be postponed to March 1. The hiring of faculty and staff and the admission of students should be handled separately after the new principal issues new contracts and announcements. During the takeover period, the takeover committee members will be responsible for all school affairs. The takeover committee members will convene meetings with various school officials within one week to plan a solution and submit it to the Ministry for approval. In addition to issuing separate orders to the school's board of directors and replying to the school, we will also notify the Shanghai Municipal Government. We are issuing a copy of the "Rules of the Temporary Takeover Committee Office of China Public School" and ordering compliance. We are also issuing an official seal for use and to demonstrate credibility. The date of use should be reported for record-keeping. You should also notify the students. This order is issued on February 5, the twentieth year of the Republic of China, by Jiang Zhongzheng, concurrently serving as Minister of Education.

▲ Rules of the Committee Office: In addition to dispatching personnel to take over the school, the Ministry of Education has also formulated a set of rules for the takeover committee's office, which were promulgated on the 5th of this month. A copy of the order was issued to each takeover committee member. The full text is recorded below: Rules of the Temporary Takeover Committee Office of China Public School (1) The Ministry of Education has established the Temporary Takeover Committee Office of China Public School (hereinafter referred to as "the Office") for the purpose of temporarily taking over and reorganizing the school's affairs until a new principal is produced and assumes office. (2) The Office shall consist of three members appointed by the Minister of Education to take over, reorganize, and preside over all school affairs. The Office shall have one permanent committee member designated by the Minister of Education from among the committee members. (3) The committee members of the Office shall come to the school daily to jointly handle school affairs. The permanent committee member shall be stationed at the school regularly. On Sundays and holidays, the committee members shall take turns or designate a representative to work at the school. (4) The committee members of the Office may convene meetings of the board of directors, faculty, and staff when necessary and may formulate various meeting rules and submit them to the Ministry of Education for record-keeping. (5) The committee members of the Office shall submit important matters to the Ministry of Education for approval before implementation. (6) The Office shall have one to two secretaries appointed by the Minister of Education from among the staff of the Ministry of Education to assist the permanent committee member in the takeover period. (7) The committee members and secretaries of the Office shall be paid by their original institutions and shall not receive additional salary from the school. However, they may be reimbursed for expenses incurred on official business, with actual receipts. (8) The Office may establish other staff positions, which shall be appointed by the permanent committee member. The number and salary of these positions shall be submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval. (9) The expenses of the Office shall be temporarily advanced by the Ministry of Education and shall be reimbursed by China Public School in the future. (10) These rules shall be promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Education. (11) The committee members and secretaries of the Office shall be relieved of their duties on the day the new principal arrives at the school, and the Office shall be dissolved at the same time.

▲ Report from Chairman Cai and Others to the Ministry of Education: On May 5, the 19th year, the Board of Directors of China Public School held a temporary meeting and elected Mr. Ma Junwu to succeed as Principal of China Public School. However, at a temporary meeting of the Board of Directors on June 8 of the same year, Principal Ma submitted his resignation due to a construction project. The attending directors declined his resignation. On October 7 of the same year, he again applied for resignation at the sixth meeting of the board of directors and was again persuaded to stay. On October 30 of the same year, the Board of Directors, due to the occurrence of disputes in the school that urgently needed to be addressed, and because Principal Ma had traveled far to Japan, had no choice but to convene a temporary meeting to discuss solutions. Yunwu had previously been entrusted by Principal Ma to submit his resignation to the directors on his behalf. The board of directors believed that Principal Ma had repeatedly expressed his intention to resign, and this time he entrusted Yunwu to submit his resignation on his behalf, and at a time when disputes were arising in the school, he had drifted away, and his intention to resign was undoubtedly firm. However, the situation in the school at that time could not be without someone responsible for reorganizing it, so it was resolved that "Principal Ma's determination to resign is acknowledged, and Mr. Yu Youren is appointed as the new principal." On November 10 of the same year, Principal Yu came to the school to inspect it once and expressed his unwillingness to take office, and sent a letter of resignation to the Chairman of the Board of Directors, but he went to Shaanxi on official business, and former Principal Ma returned to the school with him to preside over it. On January 26 of this year, the Nanjing Central Daily News and the Shanghai Shen Bao on January 27 reported that Mr. Ma told reporters that he was suffering from the lack of a successor, and he also expressed the same to the investigators sent by the Ministry. Therefore, the Standing Director and former Principal Ma negotiated and proposed that the Chairman, representing the Board of Directors, take over the school and formulate general measures. On January 31, he received a letter from former Principal Ma, stating that "after careful consideration, he felt that the situation was very unfavorable and feared that it would cause a major conflict between the students and the Board of Directors." On the same day, two so-called student representatives came to Mr. Jiemin's private residence and left a note, stating that "the entire student body has resolved that if a third party becomes the principal during this student unrest, they will swear to reject it to the death. At the same time, we do not recognize that Principal Ma has resigned," etc. Since then, the school's disputes have become more and more serious. Jiemin and others could not bear to sit idly by and had no power to maintain order, so they had no choice but to resign at a temporary meeting of the Board of Directors on the 2nd of this month. Their resignation has been accepted, and Jiemin and others have been relieved of their responsibility for China Public School. Therefore, they have prepared this document to report, and they have also recently received a respectful telegram from the Ministry inquiring about the recent developments of the Board of Directors. They have especially summarized the main points and respectfully submit them to the Ministry of Education for review. Chairman of the Board of Directors of China Public School, Cai Yuanpei, former Directors Gao Yihan, Liu Binglin, Wang Yunwu, Ding Yiyin, Yang Xingfo.

▲ Reply from the Ministry of Education to Chairman Cai and Others: Chairman Cai, and forwarded to Directors Wang Yunwu, Yang Xingfo, Gao Yihan, Liu Binglin, and Ding Yiyin, all acknowledged. The report received three days ago has been understood. The selection and re-election of the principal of a private school is the responsibility of the Board of Directors. The student unrest that has occurred at the school, with students arbitrarily expressing welcome or rejection of candidates for principal, and their actions being excessive and inappropriate, has been reported by personnel dispatched by the Ministry. It is now stated in the report that the Chairman of the Board of Directors intends to represent the Board of Directors in taking over the school, but former Principal Ma stated in a letter that "he feels that the situation is very unfavorable and fears that it will cause a major conflict between the students and the Board of Directors." Moreover, according to a letter left by student representatives, they even claimed that they would swear to oppose a third party becoming principal. Such brazen and reckless behavior, disregarding the law, and rejecting the Board of Directors' takeover, disregarding the status of the Board of Directors, cannot be tolerated under any circumstances for the sake of rectifying the school's atmosphere. The school itself has lost its basis for existence and should be disbanded immediately to rectify the academic atmosphere and maintain the rule of law. However, because the school has been established for over twenty years, it is not appropriate to allow the intentional disturbances of a few individuals to cause this historical institution to disappear. We have now appointed Gu Shusen, Cen Dezhang, and Zhu Yingpeng as temporary takeover committee members of the school to temporarily take over the school's affairs and carry out reorganization so that the Board of Directors can exercise its powers without being obstructed. The Chairman and Directors have a deep connection to the school and are expected to consider the school's future, dispel their resignation, and maintain their original intentions. The Chairman should promptly convene all directors to discuss the school's solution and re-elect a principal to take charge, so that the Ministry can show its utmost concern for the school. The request to be relieved of responsibility for China Public School should not be considered. In addition to separately ordering the school's Board of Directors, this telegram is sent to you for your information. (The text of the separate order to the Board of Directors is omitted as it is similar and redundant).
